1601 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Purtell v. Kuczek


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Montgomery County


129 Misc. 2d 166; 492 N.Y.S.2d 909; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3061



August 5, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Upon all of the above, all petitions and amended petitions are dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, candidates for the position of member of the Democratic Party county committee in various election districts within the City of Amsterdam, New York, filed designating petitions that were invalidated by respondents, the Commissioners of the Board of Elections of the County of Montgomery, New York. Several candidates filed amended petitions that were rejected by the Board. The candidates sought review of the Board's determinations.


OVERVIEW: The candidates filed designating petitions that were invalidated by the Commissioners because the insertion in the heading of each petition of the month and day as the date of the next primary election was improper and incomplete. The court held that the lack of a complete date of the primary election was a fatal defect that mandated the dismissal of the candidates' petitions. The date of the primary election was specifically prescribed by N.Y. Elect. Law § 6-132(1), and strict compliance with the content provisions of § 6-132(1) was required. A month and day, without a year, was not a date. To comply with § 6-132(1), the day, month, and year had to appear upon the petition. Notice to the candidates of the invalidity of their petitions was not required, as the invalidity was apparent on the face of the petitions. The constitutionality of § 6-132 was not before the court, as notice was not provided to the Attorney-General of the State of New York as required by N.Y. C.P.L.R. 1012(b). The amended petitions were not timely served, and N.Y. Elect. Law § 16-100 did not provide the court with authority to make such orders as justice required.


OUTCOME: The candidates' designating petitions and amended designating petitions were dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- Designating Petitions -- Incomplete Date of Primary Election

1. Designating petitions filed by petitioners, candidates for the party position of member of the county committee of the Democratic Party are invalid on the grounds that the insertion in the heading of the petition of the date of September 10 as the date when the next primary election is to be held was improper since the year 1985 did not follow September 10; Election Law § 6-132 mandates that a designating petition contain the date of the primary election, and strict compliance with the content provisions of the statute is required; "September 10" without the year 1985 is not a date; the lack of a complete date is fatal and mandates dismissal of said petitions. Moreover, petitioners Diane Morrone and Ronald Wierzbicki were properly challenged notwithstanding the fact that the objections were filed against Diane Marrone and Robert Wierzbicki; there is no contention that notice was not timely, that the required information was not set forth or that petitioners were prejudiced; further, notice to candidates is not vital [***2] when the petitions are invalid on their face.

Elections -- Designating Petitions

2. The court's determination that a designating petition was properly invalidated eliminates the issue of the propriety of an election commissioner, who is running against a candidate, ruling on said candidate's petition.

Attorney-General -- Notice of Challenge to Constitutionality of Statute

3. The issue of the constitutionality of Election Law § 6-132 is not properly before the court where no notice has been given to the Attorney-General pursuant to CPLR 1012 (b) so that his office could timely appear pursuant to Executive Law § 71 in support of the statute's constitutionality.

Elections -- Designating Petitions -- Amended Petitions -- Write-in Primary

4. Amended petitions served by petitioners, candidates for the office of member of the county committee of the Democratic Party whose original designating petitions were invalidated, requesting a write-in primary are dismissed; the amended petitions were not timely served (Election Law § 16-102 [2]), and Election Law § 16-100 does not provide the court with the authority to make such orders as justice requires.

 

1602 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Graydon


Docket No. 4N087000


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


129 Misc. 2d 265; 492 N.Y.S.2d 903; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3353



August 2, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion to dismiss is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested and charged with the crime of sexual abuse in the second degree, a class A misdemeanor. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charge against him on the ground that the information was insufficient on its face because the acts alleged did not constitute a crime. Defendant was alleged to have repeatedly rubbed the leg of an 11-year-old girl.


OVERVIEW: The information stated that defendant intentionally and repeatedly rubbed his hand on the victim's leg without authority or permission after being told not to do so. Defendant contended that the information was insufficient on its face because the leg did not constitute an "intimate part" within the meaning of N.Y. Penal Law § 130.60 and its definitional section, N.Y. Penal Law § 130.00(3). The People argued that the information was sufficient on its face and that any insufficiency was cured by alleging in a bill of particulars a touching of the inner thigh. The court found that in essence, defendant was urging the court to limit the purview of the statute to the anatomically sexual parts of the body. After examining the legislative history and prior case law, the court held that the leg was an "intimate" part of the body and that the information was sufficient on its face. The court further held that to determine if a part was "intimate", one must examine three factors: what area of the body was touched, what was the manner of the touching, and under what circumstances did the touching take place.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Sexual Abuse -- Touching "Intimate" Part of Victim's Body

An information charging defendant with sexual abuse in the second degree, alleging that he repeatedly rubbed the leg of an 11-year-old girl prior and subsequent to her demands that he cease, is sufficient on its face and need not be amended to allege that defendant stroked the girl's inner thigh, since under the circumstances presented the leg is an "intimate" part of the body; in defining "sexual contact" to be the touching of "the sexual or other intimate parts" of the victim, Penal Law § 130.00 (3) must be read broadly and not in an unduly limited fashion which would prohibit punishing certain types of physically intrusive behavior which offends society's general sense of decency, propriety and morality. Accordingly, to determine if a part of the body is "intimate", three factors must be examined: what area of the body is touched; what is the manner of touching, and under what circumstances did the touching take place.

 

1603 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cruz


Docket No. 5X002807


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Bronx County


129 Misc. 2d 235; 492 N.Y.S.2d 872; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2675



July 22, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with various A level misdemeanors, all of which were triable before a judge without a jury pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 70.15 (Reclassification Law) and N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 340.40. She filed a motion seeking an order granting a trial by jury, claiming that the Reclassification Law was unconstitutional under both the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating N.Y. Penal Law §§ 155.25, 140.15, 145.00, and 140.35. Under the Reclassification Law defendant was not entitled to a jury trial despite the fact that possible penalties included 6 months in jail and a $ 1000 fine. The court rejected a challenge to the law's constitutionality. Holding that a strong presumption of constitutionality attached to the law and that defendant was required to show unconstitutionality beyond a reasonable doubt, the court found that there was no right to a jury trial on a petty offense, that whether any particular offense carried with it the right to jury trial depended on the authorized penalty, not on the possibility of social stigma or other collateral consequences, and that neither the possible 6-month sentence nor the $ 1000 fine mandated a finding that a jury trial was required. The court also rejected defendant's equal protection challenge, holding that the statutory discrimination between first-time offenders and recidivists was not irrational and in fact was directly and rationally related to the legitimate goal of relieving demands on judicial resources.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the constitutionality of the Reclassification Law. The court denied defendant's motion in all respects.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- Right to Jury Trial -- New "Reclassification Law" Creating "Petty" A Misdemeanors

The new "Reclassification Law" (amending Penal Law § 70.15; CPL 340.40), which retains the right to jury trial for certain "serious" A misdemeanors for which the maximum authorized penalty is one year while denying the right to a jury trial for other "petty" A misdemeanors which are subject to a maximum penalty of six months' imprisonment for first offenders and a $ 1,000 fine, is not unconstitutional since the Legislature's establishment of a six-month standard is the determinative gauge of the inherent "gravity" of an offense and it would be an "improper usurpation of the legislative function" for a judge to make an independent evaluation of the seriousness of the crime to determine if a charged must be tried before a jury; the possible imposition of a $ 1,000 fine for the category of "petty" crimes does not implicate the right to a jury trial even though Federal law appears to establish a six-month/$ 500 benchmark for "petty crimes" (18 USC § 1 [3]) since the six-month benchmark is far more important than the obsolete $ 500 standard set in 1930 and the court should not disregard [***2] the clear legislative intent of the new law; the disparate treatment of first offenders and recidivists under the new law is directly and rationally related to the legitimate goal of providing speedy and inexpensive nonjury adjudications and the fact that some anomalies might result from the legislative scheme of reclassification is not sufficient to overcome the presumption of rationality that attaches to the new statute; accordingly, since defendant is charged with the "petty" crimes of petit larceny, criminal trespass in the second degree, criminal mischief in the fourth degree and possession of burglar's tools, she is not entitled to a jury trial.

 

1604 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jacobs


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Kings County


129 Misc. 2d 21; 492 N.Y.S.2d 859; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3055



July 11, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the defendants' motions are denied in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with grand larceny in the second degree and conspiracy to prevent competitive bidding on public contracts. They filed motions with the court requesting a reinspection of the grand jury minutes, and upon reinspection, to dismiss the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with knowingly and intentionally committing fraud by entering into a bidrigging scheme with a supervising buyer for the New York City Transit Authority to award defendants' company a number of contracts to sell hardware items to the Transit Authority even though it was not the lowest qualified bidder for those contracts. Defendants filed motions for reinspection of the grand jury minutes and for dismissal of the indictment on the ground that the proceedings before the grand jury were rendered defective by submission of a time-barred offense and evidence of the same, which was legally insufficient. Defendants' motions were denied. The court held that the grand jury was charged separately as to each crime and that the instructions on the law were proper. Therefore, the grand jurors understood that the two counts were distinct.


OUTCOME: The defendants' motions to dismiss were denied.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Indictment -- Evidence of Uncharged Conspiracy

1. The submission to the Grand Jury of evidence of 33 separate "overt acts" underlying a conspiracy charge that was dismissed as time barred subsequent to the Grand Jury presentation does not render defective the Grand Jury proceedings which also resulted in indictments for grand larceny in the second degree and conspiracy to prevent competitive bidding on public contracts (General Municipal law § 103-e) in relation to the alleged rigging of hardware contracts awarded by the New York City Transit Authority since evidence underlying a crime left uncharged because of the Statute of Limitations is admissible if such evidence is probative of a charged crime and each of the "overt acts" underlying the uncharged conspiracy count was probative of the substantive crimes.

Crimes -- Conspiracy to Prevent Competitive Bidding on Public Contracts -- Statute of Limitations

2. The more specific three-year Statute of Limitations is applicable to the crime of conspiracy to prevent competitive bidding on public contracts (General Municipal Law § 103-e)  [***2] rather than the two-year limitations period applicable to misdemeanors generally ( CPL 30.10) since, where a conflict exists between two applicable Statutes of Limitation, one of which is general and the other specific, the more specific statute applies and it is clear that the Legislature wanted to create a specific statute to safeguard against collusion in bidding for public contracts and intended that statute to be considered separately from the general provisions of CPL 30.10; General Municipal Law § 103-e satisfies the due process requirement that defendants be given proper notice of the charge against them since it is clear that the statute is directed toward "any person or corporation who conspires to prevent competitive bidding on a contract for public work"; the fact that defendants were also charged with criminal "conspiracy" in connection with the alleged rigging of hardware contracts awarded by the New York City Transit Authority did not prevent the grand jurors from being able to distinguish legally between the two conspiracy charges since the Grand Jury was charged separately as to each crime and the instructions on the law were proper.

 

1605 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Frankel


Docket No. 4Q014643/84


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Queens County


129 Misc. 2d 95; 492 N.Y.S.2d 671; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2685



July 8, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state charged defendant with theft of services under N.Y. Penal Law § 165.15(4) for selling an unauthorized decoding unit that intercepted and decoded television signals with the intent to avoid payment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold an unauthorized decoding unit that decoded television signals to an undercover purchaser for the state. Defendant was charged with theft of services under § 165.15(4). Defendant moved to dismiss on several grounds. The court found defendant guilty of theft of services and held that § 165.15(4) was not unconstitutional because 47 U.S.C.S. § 605 did not preempt the state from enacting legislation to deter the theft of services in the telecommunication field. The court ruled that the state had jurisdiction over defendant's offense even if the ultimate use of the decoder was to be used outside of the state. The court held that N.Y. Penal Law § 165.15(4) created a presumption that defendant sold an unauthorized decoder with the intent to avoid payment for another of the lawful charge for the service involved. The court ruled that a legal or factual impossibility defense to complete the act was not significant because, under § 165.15(4), defendant's mere attempt to sell an unauthorized decoder violated the statute. Defendant could only be found guilty of a violation and not a misdemeanor because the state did not establish a value of the service involved.


OUTCOME: The court found defendant guilty of theft of services for selling an unauthorized decoding unit that intercepted and decoded television signals with the intent to avoid payment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- Theft of Telecommunication Services -- Sale of Decoder to Intercept Cable Television Signals

1. The theft of services statute, insofar as it proscribes the sale of decoders to be used for the unauthorized interception of encoded cable television signals (Penal Law § 165.15 [4]), is not unconstitutional because of Federal preemption of the telecommunication field as it relates to defendant's 1984 sale of a decoder instrument to a private investigator and an undercover detective since the 1984 amendment to the Federal statute stating that nothing in the Federal statute is intended to prevent the States from enacting legislation to deter the theft of services in the telecommunication field (47 USC § 605), is a curative act that may be viewed as an expression of congressional intent on the issue as to the theft of services in the telecommunication field prior to the 1984 amendment and may thus be given retroactive effect.

Crimes -- Theft of Telecommunication Services -- Sale of Decoder to Intercept Cable Television Signals

2. The sale by defendant to a private investigator and an undercover police detective of a decoder instrument capable of intercepting [***2] encoded television signals violates the theft of services statute (Penal Law § 165.15 [4]) irrespective of whether the sale contemplated the use of the decoder within the State since the decoder was capable of intercepting unauthorized television signals from a cable television company providing services in New York and the sale thus had an effect in this State sufficient to confer jurisdiction to enforce the statute; proof that defendant intended to avoid payment by himself or another person of the lawful charge for telecommunication service was established beyond a reasonable doubt through the unrebutted statutory presumption that one who sells such a decoder does so with the requisite criminal intent and the fact that the decoder could also be used as a legal frequency converter does not absolve defendant from any criminality; a "legal or factual impossibility" to complete the act is of no significance and cannot reduce the crime charged to no more than an attempt to commit the crime of theft of services since a person is guilty of theft of services if he avoids or attempts to avoid payment for telecommunication services by an unauthorized decoder for sale; however, since the [***3] People failed to establish that the value of the "cable television services" involved exceeded $ 100, defendant can only be convicted of a violation rather than a misdemeanor even though this case involves transmission of telecommunication signals by microwave not cablevision inasmuch as telecommunication by microwave should be treated no differently from telecommunication by wire for purposes of the theft of services statute (see, Penal Law § 155.00 [9]).

 

1606 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kennedy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Kings County


128 Misc. 2d 937; 491 N.Y.S.2d 968; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3030



July 8, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, the court finds Penal Law § 70.06 (1) (b) (v) unconstitutional as applied to this defendant, and will sentence him as a first-time offender.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Having entered a guilty plea to robbery in the first degree, defendant challenged his status as a predicate felon and the constitutionality of N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06(1)(b)(v), which extended the 10-year period within which predicate felonies had to have been committed by a period equal to the time of defendant's confinement between the commission of those predicate felonies and the execution of sentence thereon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant denied that he was the person convicted on prior felonies as alleged by the state and contended that the tolling provisions of § 70.06(1)(b)(v) violated the Equal Protection Clause: if defendant had been able to afford to post bond following a certain arrest he would not be subject to enhanced punishment pursuant to § 70.06(1)(b)(v). The court found that the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was the individual convicted on the prior felonies. Nevertheless, the court determined to sentence defendant as a first-time offender because the court agreed that § 70.06(1)(b)(v) was unconstitutional as applied to defendant. Inclusion of the period of defendant's preconviction detention according to the tolling provisions of the predicate felony offender statute served to punish defendant in consequence of his indigency. The Equal Protection Clause was violated when an accused served more time on sentences imposed merely because he was unable to make bail due to insufficient funds.


OUTCOME: The court held in favor of the state in part, finding that defendant was the individual convicted on the prior felonies, and held in favor of defendant in part, finding that defendant should be sentenced as a first-time offender.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Sentence -- Constitutionality of Tolling Provisions of Predicate Felony Offender Statute -- Incarceration Due to Inability to Post Bond

The tolling provisions of Penal Law § 70.06 (1) (b) (v), which extend the 10-year period in which predicate felonies must have been committed in order to sentence a defendant as a predicate felony offender by adding thereto periods of defendant's incarceration which occurred between the commission of the present felony and the commission of the crimes alleged as predicates, are unconstitutional as applied to defendant whose incarceration during the subject period was due solely to his inability to post bail to secure pretrial release; increasing the punishment that defendant will have to face solely because he was financially unable to post bond after his prior arrest and was, therefore, incarcerated, violates his constitutional right to equal protection of the laws; accordingly, said period of incarceration will not serve to toll the 10-year period and defendant will be sentenced [***2] as a first-time offender.

 

1607 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


A. R. Fuels v. A. F. Supply Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


128 Misc. 2d 993; 491 N.Y.S.2d 962; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3042



July 2, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant's motion for summary judgment is granted, except that plaintiff may replead as indicated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant garnishor and plaintiff garnishee both filed motions for summary judgment on the garnishee's claim alleging that the garnishor unconstitutionally and illegally restrained more than twice the amount of a default judgment.


OVERVIEW: The garnishor recovered a default judgment against the garnishee for the sum of $ 25,568. The garnishor commenced judgment enforcement proceedings by serving a series of restraining notices pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5222 on the garnishee's banks. As a result, $ 96,372 was restrained from the garnishee's use. The court granted the garnishor's motion for summary judgment, and denied the garnishee's motion for summary judgment. The court held that the garnishee failed to make any allegation that he was not given the requisite notice of the restraining order, nor did the garnishee allege the unconstitutionality of the restraining order. The garnishee also failed to plead any allegation of malicious intent on the part of the garnishor to deprive the garnishee of its money. Absent a showing of malicious intent by the garnishor, no cause of action existed. The court granted the garnishee the right to replead its complaint.


OUTCOME: The court granted the garnishor's motion for summary judgment in the garnishee's action alleging illegal restraint of money.


HEADNOTES

Execution -- Restraining Order -- Restraint upon Twice Amount of Judgment

In an action commenced by a judgment debtor against a judgment creditor which served restraining orders on banks holding assets of plaintiff debtor, defendant creditor's motion for summary judgment shall be granted with leave granted plaintiff to replead alleging malicious intent on the part of defendant; there is no basis for plaintiff's claim that CPLR 5222, pursuant to which the restraining orders were issued, is unconstitutional simply because it permits a creditor to restrain more than twice the amount of the judgment sought to be satisfied. Malicious use of the statute does not render it unconstitutional; moreover, the statute's notice requirements minimize intrusion, as the debtor may promptly get an order directing satisfaction of the judgment and release of the balance of the restrained moneys.

 

1608 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. Egan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


129 Misc. 2d 130; 492 N.Y.S.2d 666; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2686



July 1, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers filed an action that challenged the constitutionality of a statutory funding scheme for the development of state correctional facilities pursuant to N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 11, which was dismissed on respondent Commissioner of General Service's motion for summary judgment. The taxpayers filed a motion for reargument.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted a series of statutes designed to finance the construction of new correctional facilities, collectively known as the Prison Construction Act, which authorized the State Urban Development Corporation (UDC) to issue bonds, the proceeds of which were to have been used to repay the Department of Correctional Services. The commissioner was then authorized to lease the facilities from the UDC and in turn sublet them to the department. The taxpayers filed a petition that challenged the Act's constitutionality pursuant to N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 11 on the ground that the Act incurred long-term debts on behalf of the state without voter approval. The commissioner brought a motion for summary judgment, which was granted, and the court granted the taxpayers' motion for reargument, then affirmed. The court held that the taxpayers failed to show that the state incurred long-term debt under the Act because it was the UDC that issued and was obligated under the bonds, not the State. Furthermore, § 7(1) of the Act gave the state the choice to enter into the leases with the UDC, rather than having required the state to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed their judgment that granted the commissioner's motion for summary judgment in the taxpayers' petition that challenged the constitutionality of the Prison Construction Act.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Prisons and Prisoners -- Issuance of Bonds for Prison Construction -- State Long-Term Debt without Voter Approval

Plaintiffs, although lacking taxpayer standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Prison Construction Act (L 1983, ch 56, as amended by L 1983, chs 712, 713; McKinney's Uncons Laws of NY § 6267), an elaborate funding scheme for the development of State correctional facilities including the issuance of bonds and notes by the State Urban Development Corporation (UDC) and the leaseback and eventual repurchase of correctional facilities by the State (see, New York Coalition for Criminal Justice v Coughlin, 64 NY2d 660), have standing as voters to challenge the financing scheme of the Act as violative of the constitutional prohibition against long-term State debt without voter approval (NY Const, art VII, § 11) since plaintiffs, as voters, fall within the "zone of interest"; since plaintiffs are challenging the constitutionality of the statutory financing scheme rather than any determination or action taken pursuant to the Prison Construction Act, the six-year Statute of Limitations is applicable ( CPLR 213 [1]) and not the specific 30-day limitations period [***2] established by the Act; however, on the merits, plaintiffs have failed to clearly demonstrate that the Prison Construction Act creates an unconstitutional State long-term debt without voter approval since the statute merely authorizes the State to lease correctional facilities from the UDC and does not require the State to contract a long-term debt.

 

1609 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Carmel v. Suburban Outdoor Advertising Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Putnam County


128 Misc. 2d 1065; 492 N.Y.S.2d 664; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3344



June 27, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a municipality, brought an action against defendant, an advertiser, to compel the advertiser to remove its billboard structures that were in violation of Town of Carmel, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance, §§ 323, 386.2, and 63-11A(1)(d). The advertiser argued that the Town of Carmel, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance violated its First Amendment free speech rights. The matter was submitted for determination.


OVERVIEW: Town of Carmel, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance, §§ 323, 386.2, and 63-11A(1)(d) had the effect of banning billboards within the limits of the Town of Carmel, N.Y., except for those that advertised products or services dispensed at the place where the billboard was located. All preexisting non-compliant billboards had to be removed within two years from the date of enactment of the Town of Carmel, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance. The advertiser had three billboard structures within the Town's limits at locations not falling within those proscribed by the Town of Carmel, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance. The court held that Town of Carmel, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance § 386.2, which limited billboards to the place of business, and Town of Carmel, N.Y., Zoning Ordinance § 63-11A(1)(d), which required removal of pre-existing non-compliant billboards, were unconstitutional and, thus, unenforceable. Though the town had the authority to regulate billboards for the purposes of protecting the public health and safety or for aesthetic purposes alone, it had to do so in a manner that did not infringe on the advertiser's First Amendment rights. The Town did not do so.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the Town's complaint.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Regulation of Billboards

A town zoning ordinance which has the effect of banning billboards within town limits except for those which advertised products for services dispensed at the location where the billboard was located, and provided that the prohibited billboards were to be removed within two years of the effective date of the ordinance, is unconstitutional and unenforceable; it is an unconstitutional infringement on an individual's right to freedom of expression to prohibit an on-site occupant from displaying a message other than that relating to goods and services dispensed at that location.

 

1610 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Lenario v. Ward


INDEX No. 7659/85, Cal. No. 44


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


129 Misc. 2d 326; 492 N.Y.S.2d 985; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2709



June 24, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a lessee of property (lessee), filed an application pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, against respondent, the Police Commissioner of the City of New York (commissioner), challenging the constitutionality of the Padlock Law, New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code §§ 436-8.0, 436-8.1 (1984), and the regulations promulgated thereunder.


OVERVIEW: The lessee's premises was ordered closed by the commission pursuant to the Padlock Law and the regulations promulgated thereunder. The lessee admitted running a numbers operation out of the premises but contended that gambling should not be illegal and that it did not constitute a public nuisance. The lessee filed a petition pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 challenging the constitutionality of the Padlock Law on the grounds that it violated his due process rights in that he was deprived of property rights by unduly repressive means not substantially related to achieving legitimate governmental ends. The court rejected the lessee's claims. The court rejected the lessee's claims and ruled that the Padlock Law and regulations carefully protected individual rights by providing for notice of arrests and of proceedings, so that the lessee could abate the suspected nuisance and that ignorance of the offenses, or nonparticipation therein, was not a defense.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the lessee's petition challenging the constitutionality of the Padlock Law and regulations promulgated thereunder.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional Law -- Validity of "Padlock Law"

Petitioner's application challenging the constitutionality of the Padlock Law (Administrative Code of City of New York §§ 436-8.0, 436-8.1) and the regulations promulgated thereunder, which authorize the Police Commissioner to impose sanctions for public nuisances, including the possible closure of a premises when property is used in violation of penal law such as those relating to prostitution, gambling and drugs is dismissed, since the Padlock Law is a proper exercise of the State's police power in that it is designed to promote the general societal welfare and its enforcement provisions are reasonably related to the stated objectives of the Padlock Law, it does not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws as it is civil in nature and does not punish conduct but is aimed at nuisance abatement, it protects due process rights as the regulations carefully protect individual rights by providing for notice of arrests and of proceedings so that an owner or lessee can abate the suspected nuisance and the Padlock Law's presumption of continuing illegal activity arising from two or more convictions in the previous year, coupled [***2] with an arrest within 30 days of a Padlock Law hearing, is based on a rational connection between a proven fact and a presumed fact; furthermore, the fact that here the hearing officer was an employee of the police department does not render him constitutionally unacceptable since petitioner has shown no evidence to back up his assertion that this procedure resulted in the hearing officer being biased.

 

1611 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rochester Gas & Electric Corp. v. Public Service Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


128 Misc. 2d 801; 490 N.Y.S.2d 956; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3001



June 20, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner gas corporation instituted an action seeking a declaratory judgment that an application of respondent, the Public Service Commission of New York (PSC), of N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 66-d(2) violated the gas corporation's right to due process. PSC filed a motion for an order converting the action into a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding and for summary judgment. The gas corporation cross-moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The gas corporation purchased, distributed, and sold natural gas to customers. It did not provide gas transportation within its service territory. The PSC issued an opinion ordering distribution companies to file transportation tariffs. The legislature then enacted § 66-d(2) which required gas corporations to transport or contract with others to transport customer-owned gas at just and reasonable rates. The PSC conducted a formal evidentiary hearing then issued a final opinion and order requiring the utilities, including the gas corporation, to file gas transportation leaves. The gas corporation asserted that § 66-d(2) interfered with its right to use and enjoy its property, and converted it into a common carrier by requiring it to hold itself out for the transportation of customer-owned gas. The court held that the gas corporation failed to meet its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that § 66-d was unconstitutional. Section 66-d was a proper exercise of the State's authority to enact reasonable measures controlling the use of utility property to safeguard the public interest. The court would not substitute its judgment for that of the PSC.


OUTCOME: The court denied the gas corporation's motion for a preliminary injunction and granted the PSC's motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint. The gas corporation's cross-motion for summary judgment was denied.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Public Utilities -- Requiring Gas Corporations to Transport Customer-Owned Gas -- Validity of Statute

 Public Service Law § 66-d (2), which requires gas corporations to transport or contract with others to transport customer-owned gas at just and reasonable rates following notice and a hearing, does not violate petitioner gas corporation's right to due process; the statute carefully limits a utility's transportation obligations and, in so doing, makes transportation service subservient to the demands of other end users; section 66-d (2) directs utilities to serve only large volume users, and even then, to do so only when the company has available capacity and transportation will not impair its ability to render adequate service to its customers; further, the State may enact reasonable measures controlling the use of utility property to safeguard the public interest, and this statute represents a rational and lawful exercise of the Legislature's authority to regulate the use of utility property.

 

1612 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Lazarus v. Steingut


Index No.: 12894/84, No. 178


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


129 Misc. 2d 982; 494 N.Y.S.2d 930; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2889



June 17, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners employees, who were attorneys in the Workers' Compensation Board (WCB), filed a declaratory judgment action to declare that respondents, the chairman of the WCB and the general counsel of the WCB, could not restrict or prohibit the employees from engaging in private law practice. Respondents filed a motion to dismiss the employee's action.


OVERVIEW: The employees engaged in private practice of law during their off-duty hours and when they formed a partnership, the general counsel issued a memorandum that restricted their private practice. Subsequently, the chairman prohibited any attorney employed by the WCB from engaging in the private practice of law. The employees argued that memorandum and order were unconstitutional, in excess of respondents' jurisdiction, and violated the Workers' Compensation Law, the Public Officers Law and the Civil Service Law. In granting the motion to dismiss, the court held that N.Y. Workers' Comp. Law § 152 permitted the chairman to make, amend, and repeal regulations for the administration of the WCB and its employees. Respondents determined that the employees' private practice of law posed a potential conflict between private interests and public service. The prohibition against private practice of law was within respondents' power to regulate employment.


OUTCOME: The court granted respondents' motion to dismiss the employees' declaratory judgment action.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Workers' Compensation -- Workers' Compensation Board -- Power to Restrict Employees from Private Practice of Law

It is within the power of the Chairman of the Workers' Compensation Board, by administrative regulation, to restrict petitioner attorneys employed by the Board from the private practice of law; Workers' Compensation Law § 152, which permits the Chairman to make, amend and repeal regulations for the administration of the Board and its employees, confers upon the Chairman the authority to so regulate outside employment; moreover, such restriction does not violate Judiciary Law § 90, which vests the power to regulate the private practice of law solely in the Appellate Division, since it regulates petitioners' employment, not the private practice of law.

 

1613 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Cherry v. Koch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


129 Misc. 2d 346; 491 N.Y.S.2d 934; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3069



June 17, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prostitute and petitioner patron sought a judgment from the Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County (New York), declaring certain state penal laws unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, prostitute and patron, sought a judgment declaring N.Y. Penal Law §§ 230.00 and 230.03, which prohibited prostitution and patronizing a prostitute, unconstitutional. The court held that petitioners failed to present the necessary requirements for a declaratory judgment and dismissed the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. However, the court reviewed the merits of the complaint due to the importance of the issues to the criminal justice system and because it presented a recurring problem. The court held that the statutes did not violate due process or equal protection rights under the United States and New York Constitutions. The court held that commercial sexual activity did not come within the sphere of protected privacy. The court held that there was no recognized fundamental right to engage in commercial sex or prostitution and that there was a rational relationship between the statutes and legitimate state interests. The court held that equal protection was not violated because there was a marital exemption for the crime of prostitution and there was a rational basis to discriminate between married and unmarried persons under the statutes.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioners' amended complaint seeking a declaratory judgment for failure to state a cause of action.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Courts -- Law of the Case

1. The doctrine of law of the case is applicable to rulings made on the merits and unrelated to the pleadings; thus, in an action seeking a judgment declaring Penal Law §§ 230.00 and 230.03 unconstitutional where the complaint was previously dismissed by a different judge for failure to state a cause of action with leave to replead, the prior ruling that petitioners possess standing and present a justiciable controversy are the law of the case; however, law of the case is not applicable to the issue of whether a declaratory judgment is available to petitioners since the propriety of a declaratory judgment in the action was never decided, and leave to replead was specifically granted so that petitioners could amplify the factual basis for declaratory relief.

Declaratory Judgments -- When Remedy Appropriate

2. An amended complaint by petitioners, a prostitute and a patron, seeking a judgment declaring unconstitutional Penal Law §§ 230.00 and 230.03, which prohibit prostitution and patronizing a prostitute, is dismissed for failure to state a cause of action; petitioners have not presented the necessary requirements for a declaratory judgment;  [***2] they have not been threatened with prosecution, do not allege any irreparable injury, past or future, and have not presented the court with either a sole question of law or undisputed set of facts; moreover, to hold that petitioners, who are in the same position as every criminal currently contemplating criminal activity, can avail themselves of a declaratory judgment regarding their future criminal activity would be onerous and burdensome and would remove from the criminal court the power to decide the criminal constitutionality of a criminal statute.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Prostitution -- Patronizing Prostitute

3. Penal Law §§ 230.00 and 230.03, which prohibit prostitution and patronizing a prostitute, are not unconstitutional; where commerce is involved, such as the payment of a fee, personal sexual activity, whether done privately or publicly, does not come within the sphere of the right to privacy; inasmuch as there is no recognized fundamental right to engage in commercial sex or prostitution and since, given the strong presumption of validity accorded legislative enactments and the evils associated with prostitution, it cannot be said that sections [***3] 230.00 and 230.03 are irrational or bear no rational relationship to valid State interests, the statutes do not violate due process; moreover, equal protection is not violated by existence of the marital exemption to the prostitution statutes since an expanded zone of privacy attaches to the marital relationship and it is that special status that provides a rational basis to discriminate between married and unmarried persons and, in addition, all the attendant evils associated with commercial sex are simply not present when sexual conduct occurs between a married couple; that section 230.03 discriminates between those who keep mistresses and those who patronize prostitutes does not constitute a violation of equal protection since the lover-mistress relationship lacks most of the evils perceived by the Legislature as attendant to prostitution.

 

1614 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Byrnes v. County of Monroe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Rochester


128 Misc. 2d 700; 490 N.Y.S.2d 977; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2982



June 10, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By order to show cause, petitioner attorney sought an order of enforcement or other proper relief against respondent County of Monroe (county) in respect to an award of counsel fees and disbursements the court granted the attorney for his representation of an indigent criminal defendant.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was appointed to represent an indigent criminal defendant because the Public Defender's office had a conflict of interest. The court awarded attorney fees exceeding the sum allowed by N.Y. County Law § 722-b (the statute), save but for "extraordinary circumstances," which the court found existed. The county did not pay the attorney. The court held that N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit.22, § 1022.12 (the rule) was irreconcilable with the statute because the statute's certain inclusion of the trial court as the sole authority to provide for compensation in excess of statutory limits excluded the Supervising Judge of the Criminal Courts for the Seventh Judicial District. The statute had supremacy and the rule was unconstitutional. Failure to secure approval of the supervising judge was not fatal. No notice of claim was required under N.Y. County Law § 52. The statute authorized a special proceeding to enforce the award, which was properly commended by order to show cause, and a plenary action was not required. The court granted summary judgment for the attorney because no issues of fact, except for fraud, were available to the county.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the county's affirmative defenses and granted summary judgment in favor of the attorney for the counsel fees and disbursements the county owed the attorney.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Attorney and Client -- Compensation -- Assigned Counsel for Criminal Defendants

A rule of the Appellate Division, Fourth Department (22 NYCRR 1022.12 [b]), requiring that "the Supervising Judge of the Criminal Courts of the appropriate judicial district" approve any request for counsel fees in excess of the statutory limits established for attorneys assigned as defense counsel under County Law § 722-b, is unconstitutional and void for being inconsistent and irreconcilable with the clear statutory mandate of County Law § 722-b giving the trial court the sole authority to provide for compensation and disbursements in excess of the statutory limits in all cases of "extraordinary circumstances" without interference from any auditing agency or administrative overseer; since a claim against the County for counsel fees fixed by the court is contractual, the notice of claim requirements of County Law § 52 for tort claims is inapplicable; enforcement of an award of counsel fees may be by way of a special proceeding commenced by order to show cause ( CPLR 403) rather than by a plenary action; accordingly, in view of petitioner's "protracted representation" following the disqualification [***2] of the Public Defender's office due to a conflict of interest and the complex collateral issues involved in defense of the misdemeanor charges, petitioner is awarded $ 993 plus interest for counsel fees and disbursements.

 

1615 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Roth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Suffolk County


129 Misc. 2d 381; 492 N.Y.S.2d 971; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2738



June 3, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought dismissal by the court of various charges upon multiple claims that the list of hazardous wastes and criminal sanctions pursuant to N.Y. Environmental Conservation Law § 27-0903, 6 N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 366.4, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The defendant owned an airplane refurbishing business. The defendant unlawfully disposed of waste resulting from the painting and stripping process in violation of N.Y. Environmental Conservation Law (ECL) § 27-0903, and charges upon multiple claims were brought against the defendant. The defendant contended that the Commissioner's failure to hold a public hearing pursuant to ECL § 3-0301 rendered the list of hazardous wastes unconstitutional. The court held that there was no finding of unconstitutionality where the statute could have been read to give its ambiguous language a meaning that could have stood without conflict with the fundamental law. In addition, the court held that, pursuant to ECL § 3-0301(2)(m), in order for the Commissioner to have fulfilled his mandate of insuring the quality of the environment (ECL § 1-0101) he was authorized to adopt such rules, regulations and procedures as was necessary, convenient or desirable to effectuate the purposes of the chapter. Finally, where a Commissioner was mandated to adopt federal regulations as part of a state's own regulations he could do so, without public hearing, pursuant to ELC § 21 3-0301(2)(m).


OUTCOME: The court rendered judgment in favor of the state and did not dismiss the charges against the defendant as unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- List of Hazardous Wastes

1. Where the Commissioner of Environmental Conservation is mandated to adopt Federal regulations as part of the State's own regulations, he may do so, without public hearing, pursuant to ECL 3-0301 (2) (m); thus, 6 NYCRR 366.4 (a) through (d), which were promulgated on February 1, 1984 by the Commissioner of Environmental Conservation without prior public hearing pursuant to ECL 3-0301 (2) (m) and which copy the Federal list of hazardous wastes, are not unconstitutional; inasmuch as Congress chose to preempt the States from establishing less stringent rules than the minimum Federal ecological standards, the Commissioner was mandated to adopt, as a minimum, the Federal list of hazardous wastes; thus, with respect to 6 NYCRR 366.4 (a) through (d), the holding of public hearings in New York would have been meaningless and repetitive since such hearings were originally mandated as a condition precedent to the adoption of the Federal list.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Unlawful Disposal of Hazardous Wastes

2. A finding that a statute is unconstitutional is not mandated where the statute [***2] in question can be read to give its ambiguous language a meaning that may stand without conflict with the fundamental law; thus, ECL 71-2713 (7), which proscribes the knowing disposal of more than 1,500 gallons or 15,000 pounds, whichever is less, of an aggregate weight of hazardous wastes without authorization, is not unconstitutionally vague for failure to define or fix the time frame in which the illegal act must be committed since the statute may be interpreted to permit the prosecution of a single disposal in excess of 1,500 gallons, or an aggregated disposal in excess of 1,500 gallons where the aggregation results from wastage related to various stages of a single job or the wastage from several jobs all occurring at the same place and time; moreover, the use of the term "aggregate weight" in ECL 71-2713 (7) does not render the statute unconstitutional as being overbroad; accordingly, the count of an indictment against defendant which aggregates separate allegedly illegal disposals unrelated by job, place or time, is dismissed.

 

1616 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Millson v. Manfredo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Oneida County


128 Misc. 2d 546; 490 N.Y.S.2d 446; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2956



May 31, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Respondent's motion to dismiss is therefore denied and the matter will be scheduled in this court for disposition only.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father filed a motion to dismiss the paternity petition of petitioner mother upon the grounds that more than five years had elapsed between the date of the child's birth and the date the petition was filed and, therefore, the petition was barred by N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 517.


OVERVIEW: The mother conceded that the application of § 517 would have barred the petition. However, the mother contended that § 517 was unconstitutional because the statute provided shorter limitation periods for mothers who brought paternity proceedings from that for fathers who brought paternity proceedings and thus denied the mother equal protection under the law. Because the mother and the adjudicated father of a child born out of wedlock had equal rights in relation to their child, the court could find no basis for providing different periods during which each might assert its rights. The state's interest in avoiding stale or fraudulent claims could be equally served by a gender-neutral statute. Where the state's compensatory and ameliorative purposes were as well served by a gender-neutral classification as one that gender classified and therefore carried with it the baggage of sexual stereotypes, the state could not be permitted to classify on the basis of sex. The motion to dismiss was denied.


OUTCOME: The father's motion to dismiss the mother's paternity action was denied.


HEADNOTES

Children Born out of Wedlock -- Paternity Proceeding -- Limitations Period

Family Court Act § 517 (a), which provides for a five-year limitations period for paternity proceedings commenced by the mother of an illegitimate child, is unconstitutional and, while no determination is made as to the proper period, it is not less than the 10-year period given to public welfare officials; consequently, the instant proceeding, commenced some six and one-half years after the birth of the child, is timely. Petitioner's attack on the statute's constitutionality succeeds because the mother and father of a child born out of wedlock have equal rights in relation to their child and a declaration of paternity encompasses much more than simply ordering support; therefore, there is no justification for providing different limitations periods for mothers as for fathers, who may wait until just prior to the child's 18th birthday to bring a proceeding, and the State's interest in avoiding stale or fraudulent claims can be equally served by a gender-neutral statute. Inasmuch [***2] as scientific advances have ameliorated many of the problems of proof in paternity cases, where a disparity exists between differing limitations periods, the longer, not the shorter, period should apply.

 

1617 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Association of Commercial Property Owners v. New York City Loft Bd.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


128 Misc. 2d 370; 490 N.Y.S.2d 113; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2914



May 30, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought to annul a regulation adopted by respondent New York City Loft Board mandating the same minimum heating standards for interim multiple dwellings as were required for other residential units in New York City. Petitioners alleged the regulation was arbitrary, capricious, and unconstitutional because it did not include a cost pass-along for increased fuel expenses.


OVERVIEW: The New York Loft Law, N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 280 et seq., was enacted to meet the emergency situation created by the number of commercial and manufacturing buildings being converted into residential use without compliance with applicable building codes. The New York City Loft Board was created by this law and pursuant to its statutory authority, it enacted rules and regulations relating to the minimum housing maintenance standards for interim multiple dwellings. Petitioners alleged that the regulation relating to heating was constitutional infirm as it did not include pass along costs for the owners' increased fuel expenses. The court dismissed petitioners' claim and ruled that the regulations were constitutional. The court held that the Board had authority to pass the regulations and its failure to include a cost pass-along was neither arbitrary nor capricious. The court noted that the costs would eventually be passed along in rent adjustments after the properties were in compliance with the N.Y. Multiple Dwelling Law. Indeed the court held petitioners' allegations were inconsistent with the specific legislative intent in the law, New York public policy, and national policy.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioners' claim that sought the annulment of a regulation by the Loft Board.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Regulation of Loft Board

1. In a proceeding challenging the constitutionality of a regulation issued by the New York City Loft Board, petitioners' threshold procedural attack that the Board failed to make a specific finding of a special emergency before issuing the regulation is meritless; as the Legislature itself described the emergency which prompted the enactment of the enabling legislation, it would be duplicative to require the Loft Board to make a new finding of an emergency each time it enacts a regulation.

Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Constitutionality

2. The Loft Law withstands constitutional challenge since it was enacted in response to an emergency situation created by illegal loft conversions; the means selected by the Legislature to remedy those conversion problems were reasonable in light of policy considerations to prompt owners of buildings containing converted lofts to bring their buildings into compliance with applicable health and safety codes.

Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Constitutionality of Regulation Requiring Owners to Provide Heat without Rent Increases

3. A regulation of the New [***2] York City Loft Board which requires owners to provide heat for their tenants is neither unconstitutional, nor arbitrary and capricious, and is consistent with the State's public policy of improving the health and safety of loft tenants; although the regulation in question does not contain a pass-along provision whereby landlords could immediately recover the costs of supplying heat, the Loft Law does provide a mechanism to recover such costs since a landlord may include such costs when applying to the Board for a rent adjustment after bringing his building into compliance with all relevant codes, thereby creating an incentive for an owner to bring his building into compliance. Furthermore, an otherwise valid regulation is not invalidated merely because it imposes financial burdens on certain parties.

 

1618 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Enki Properties, N. v. v. Loft Bd. of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


128 Misc. 2d 485; 489 N.Y.S.2d 841; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2947



May 23, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Loft Board of the City of New York (board) determined that petitioner building owner's premises were an interim multiple dwelling as defined by N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 7-C. The owner filed an action against the board to challenge the constitutionality of § 7-C. The court entertained the owner's motion to annul the board's determination and a motion by residential tenants who sought leave to intervene.


OVERVIEW: The tenant applied to the board for classification under § 7-C because the law protected the health, safety, and welfare or residential tenants by enforcing residential building code regulations on such property pursuant to N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 280. The court found that the law afforded the landlord procedural due process, which included notice and access to a full and fair hearing, the right to call and cross-examine witnesses, and the right to adduce and rebut evidence. In holding that the New York Loft Law was constitutional, the court found that the law did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because the legislature created a classification based on legitimate state concerns, not one that was arbitrary. The court held that loft owners were singled out because their buildings posed fire and safety code violations and the owners often colluded with tenants to bring about the conditions that the law sought to correct. Further, the court found that the Loft Law did not violate U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, because it did not improperly impair contracts between landlords and tenants. Every contract was subject to the lawful exercise of the police power.


OUTCOME: The court denied the owner's motion to annul the board's determination that the premises were subject to safety regulations. The court denied as moot the named residential tenants who sought leave to intervene.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Constitutionality

1. Petitioner's landlord's attack on the constitutionality of the Loft Law (Multiple Dwelling Law art 7-C), in which the assertion is made that the law will cause tenants to flee their residences if the Loft Board grants landlords' requested increases in rent, or that the Board will fail to properly increase rents, thereby resulting in a diminution of the value of their premises in either event, is without factual foundation, based on sheer speculation, and flies in the face of the fact that New York City is experiencing one of the lowest residential vacancy rates in its history.

Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Constitutionality

2. Although the Loft Law (Multiple Dwelling Law art 7-C) may be burdensome to owners of buildings subject to its strictures, it is not constitutionally infirm on the grounds that it destroys the value of said buildings, since a landlord may still operate his building, pass along his costs and receive an economic return; although petitioner landlord contends that the law will make the New York City housing crisis more severe, it is sufficient to note that if it is the finding of the [***2] Legislature that the law will alleviate the crisis it is not for the court to find otherwise, since it is beyond cavil that the interests addressed by the statute, housing safety and health, are legitimate ones, and even a cursory examination of the specific provisions of the law show them to be reasonably related to the ends sought to be achieved. Consequently the court may not challenge the Legislature's acumen or second-guess the efficacy of the remedy chosen.

Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Constitutionality

3. The Loft Law (Multiple Dwelling Law art 7-C) does not unconstitutionally regulate commercial rents since the statute is silent as to what would happen should a tenant use a portion of his residence for other purposes; although there is no denying that the landlord may, in some situations, be forced to charge less than the commercial market rate for space which is being used commercially, this result occurs as the incidental by-product of processes which are completely independent, i.e., neither encouraged nor discouraged, by the law. Moreover, the tenant who seeks to abuse the statute and uses an inconsequential portion of his unit for residential purposes [***3] may not be covered by the law.

Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Constitutionality

4. The fact that the Legislature may have slighted a landlord's interest with respect to a loft unit which is being used for both residential and commercial purposes in its enactment of the Loft Law (Multiple Dwelling Law art 7-C), does not render the law unconstitutional since the Legislature had the right to act as it did, and the court shall not substitute its own judgment or the desires of litigants as alternatives to solutions given the force of law by the Legislature. Thus, that a landlord may be receiving less than the market rate for commercial properties in situations in which a portion of residential premises is being used commercially weighs only as to the equities of the statute, and not as to its constitutionality. Moreover, the same argument applies to petitioner's complaint that the resale value of his investment has been diminished and that he will not be able to obtain his expected rate of return on his investment, since there is no constitutionally guaranteed rate of return on investment.

Landlord and Tenant -- Loft Law -- Constitutionality

5. The Loft Law [***4] (Multiple Dwelling Law art 7-C) does not violate US Constitution, article I, § 10 (1) because the statute is reasonable and necessary to serve an important and legitimate purpose for the general welfare; thus, although the statute may be said to impair contracts between landlords and tenants, it does not do so improperly because every contract is made subject to the lawful exercise of the police power. Neither is the statute violative of the equal protection clause: owners of commercial buildings which now house residential tenants are singled out because their buildings present particular problems in terms of fire and safety code violations, and because they have brought about extensive litigation, and have often colluded with tenants to bring about the conditions sought to be remedied. Therefore, it is entirely rational that landlords who benefited from an influx of residential tenants now be made to pay the costs stemming from the presence of those tenants so that they may continue their residence in safety. Finally, the statute affords building owners procedural due process in providing them notice of and access to a full and fair hearing, the right to call and cross-examine [***5] witnesses, and to adduce and rebut evidence.

 

1619 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Slutzky v. Cuomo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Albany County


128 Misc. 2d 365; 490 N.Y.S.2d 427; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2913



May 21, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief with respect to an agreement between the Department of Environmental Conservation (DEC) and the New York State Olympic Regional Development Authority (ORDA) for the management of Gore Mountain Ski Center. The citizen alleged that N.Y. Const. art. XIV, § 1, the "forever wild" provision, prohibited the lease of the public facilities to ORDA.


OVERVIEW: The court held that (1) the citizen had standing pursuant to N.Y. State Fin. Law art. 7-A, to bring an action for equitable or declaratory relief against an officer or employee who was causing or was about to cause a wrongful expenditure or disbursement of state funds or property; (2) a six-year, rather than a four-month, statute of limitations applied to claims against officials premised on constitutional prohibitions; (3) laches did not apply without delay and prejudice; (4) ORDA was a public benefit corporation created by the legislature and directed by it to use its powers to manage the ski center; (5) the "forever wild" provision authorized the construction and maintenance of the ski center, but prohibited the state from permitting others, whether corporations or individuals, except as agents of the state, to operate the facilities; (6) the complaint, construed favorably to the citizen, stated a claim; (7) the agreement was void if it was a lease, but it was valid if it was an agency agreement; (8) the right of control was essential for an agency relationship; and (9) the state retained control over ORDA in the management of the center, so there was a valid agency agreement.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motions to dismiss based on the statute of limitations, laches, and failure to state a claim. The court declared that the agreement between the state DEC and ORDA was lawful, constitutional and valid.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Limitation of Actions -- Six-Year Statute of Limitations -- Laches -- Action Based upon "Forever Wild" Provision of State Constitution

1. An action to vacate an agreement between the State Department of Environmental Conservation and the State Olympic Regional Development Authority on the ground that it constitutes a lease of State forest lands in contravention of the "forever wild" provision of NY Constitution, article XIV, § 1, is governed by a six-year, rather than four-month, Statute of Limitations since the instant action seeks declarative and injunctive relief premised upon certain constitutional prohibitions (see, New York Public Interest Research Groups v Levitt, 62 AD2d 1074). In addition, the action is not barred by the doctrine of laches since there has been no significant delay which has prejudiced defendants, who have had ample notice of the challenge to the agreement, and cannot be heard to assert any feigned surprise by receipt of process.

Environmental Conservation -- State Forest Lands -- Prohibition against Leasing -- Stating Cause of Action

2. The complaint in an action to vacate an agreement between the State Department of Environmental [***2] Conservation and the State Olympic Regional Development Authority on the ground that it constitutes a lease of State forest lands in contravention of the "forever wild" provision of the NY Constitution, article XIV, § 1, validly asserts a cause of action since it gives notice of the transactions relied upon by plaintiff and asserts material elements of a cause of action to enforce a constitutional provision; therefore, defendants' motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action must be denied.

Environmental Conservation -- State Forest Lands -- Prohibition against Leasing

3. An agreement between the State Department of Environmental Conservation (DEC) and the State Olympic Regional Development Authority (ORDA) whereby the latter would "operate, maintain and manage the Gore Mountain ski center", does not violate the "forever wild" provision of NY Constitution, article XIV, § 1 which prohibits the leasing of State forest lands, since the agreement merely establishes an agency relationship concerning the management of the ski center: DEC has not relinquished control over the center; DEC retains the right to conduct inspections, announced or not, at its sole discretion [***3] (a right completely at odds with the concept of a leasehold estate); no capital improvements may be made to the facilities without approval of DEC; ORDA, in its management capacity, shall be held harmless from any liability arising in connection with the agreement; and the provisions for termination recognize that either party may abrogate the agreement upon the happening of specified events, thereby reaffirming the requirement of mutual consent during the tenure of the principal/agent relationship.

 

1620 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


129 Misc. 2d 851; 491 N.Y.S.2d 545; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3091



May 10, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly the Attorney-General is directed to settle a judgment declaratory of the following: (1) Department of Personnel Policy and Procedure Memorandum No. 544-84 was lawfully issued; (2) rejection of a veteran's credit to plaintiffs was valid and in compliance with law; (3) that so much of NY Constitution, article V, § 6 as requires State residency of an applicant at the time an eligible civil service list is established as a condition for an award of a veteran's bonus points is valid and not in conflict with Federal constitutional law; and (4) that so much of NY Constitution, article V, § 6 as requires State residency of an applicant at the time of induction into the armed services as a condition for an award of a veteran's bonus points is null and void as in conflict with Federal constitutional law.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, officers of the New York City Housing Authority Police Department (HAPD), and residents of New Jersey, filed a motion for summary judgment against defendant New York City in the officers' action challenging the denial of veteran's credit for purposes of promotion on the ground that the officers were not residents of New York at the time the promotional list was established.


OVERVIEW: The officers contended that the city's denial of veteran credits contravened N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 85(1)(a), the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the federal and state constitutions, the Privileges And Immunities Clause, the fundamental right to travel, and a certain order of the court and arbitrarily and irrationally discriminated against them. The court held in favor of the city. A state could constitutionally require local residence as a condition of entry level public employment. A fortiori, if a state could require a policeman, fireman, or other public employee to be a resident as an absolute condition of employment, it could legitimately adopt the far less coercive policy of favoring a resident veteran over a nonresident one who was seeking a supervisory promotion from the ranks. Therefore, so much of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6 as required state residency of an applicant at the time an eligible civil service list was established as a condition for an award of a veteran's bonus points was valid and the denial of veterans' credit to the officers was valid and in compliance with law.


OUTCOME: The court denied the officers' motion for summary judgment and entered a declaratory judgment holding that the denial of a veteran's credit to nonresident veterans was lawful.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Appointment and Promotion -- State Residency Requirement for Veterans' Credits

The denial of veterans' credits for purposes of promotion by the New York City Personnel Department to all persons who were not residents of New York State at the time the promotional list was established is not unlawful since, although Civil Service Law § 85 (2) (a) (2)  [***2] does not require that a veteran be a resident of the State "at the time of application for appointment or promotion" in order to be eligible for a veteran's credit, the statute is contrary to the constitutional requirement for a veteran's credit of State residence at both the time of entrance into the Armed Forces and at the time of the establishment of an eligible list (NY Const, art V, § 6) and, therefore, invalid; although so much of NY Constitution, article V, § 6 as requires State residency of an applicant at the time of induction into the armed services as a condition for an award of veterans' bonus points is null and void for conflicting with Federal constitutional law, the requirement of State residency of an applicant at the time an eligible civil service list is established as a condition for an award of veterans' bonus points is valid and not in conflict with Federal constitutional law since a State may constitutionally require that a public employee be a resident as an absolute condition of employment and may thus legitimately adopt the far less coercive policy of favoring a resident veteran over a nonresident one who is seeking a supervisory promotion from the ranks.

 

1621 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Gabriel M.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Kings County


128 Misc. 2d 313; 488 N.Y.S.2d 1007; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2901



May 2, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother filed a motion for a preliminary hearing on the issue of vacatur of an adjournment in contemplation of dismissal (ACD) as a statutory condition precedent to petitioner, Commissioner of the Department of Social Services, being allowed to proceed to plenary hearing on the merits of an underlying petition charging neglect.


OVERVIEW: The mother was allegedly unable to care for her children because of mental disability for which she had refused medication. The matter was adjourned in contemplation of dismissal upon certain specific conditions, including a requirement that the mother continue in therapy and cooperate with supervision by the Commissioner. A petition alleging violation of the ACD was filed. The second sentence of Fam. Ct. Act § 1039(e), which provided for disposition of a petition upon a deeming of neglect, was struck down as constitutionally offensive. The mother argued that the requirement of a hearing prior to restoration existed independently of the second sentence of § 1039(e). The court disagreed and denied the requested hearing. To require proof of two separate sets of allegations where one ordinarily sufficed simply because an act of prosecutorial grace was extended was manifest absurdity. In no event could the court construe decisional law to require that a hearing be held simply to confer upon a petitioning child protective agency the right to prosecute its original case on the merits, a right incidentally, which was a statutory mandate under Fam. Ct. Act § 1032.


OUTCOME: The court denied the mother's motion for a hearing.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Parent and Child -- Abused or Neglected Child -- Vacatur of Adjournment in Contemplation of Dismissal

The Family Court is not required to conduct a preliminary hearing prior to vacating an adjournment in contemplation of dismissal (ACD) in a neglect proceeding as a condition precedent to proceeding with a plenary hearing on the merits of the underlying neglect petition since the statutory provision calling for a hearing prior to vacatur of an ACD was inextricably connected with the major provisions in the same statute found unconstitutional by the Court of Appeals (see, Matter of Marie B., 62 NY2d 352) whereby neglect was "deemed to exist" upon proof of violation of the terms of the ACD without any proof of actual neglect (Family Ct Act § 1039 [e]) and requiring that a hearing be held simply to confer upon the petitioning child protective agency the right to prosecute its original case on the merits, a right which is a statutory mandate, would result in a manifest absurdity; accordingly, the ACD is vacated and the case restored for trial on the merits.

 

1622 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hall


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


128 Misc. 2d 166; 489 N.Y.S.2d 140; 1985 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3351



April 24, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's motion is denied in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in a misdemeanor information with petit larceny. Defendant sought an order directing that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 340.40(2) was unconstitutional or, in the alternative, that the charges be tried before a jury.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 340.40(2) was amended by 1984 N.Y.
