Petitioner landlord may not enjoin a tenants' association from soliciting additional members and collecting and holding the rent moneys of its members during a rent strike organized to protest conditions in the building since the tenants' association acted legally in holding rent moneys that the individual tenants would have a right to withhold because of the landlord's violation of the warranty of habitability (Real Property Law, § 235-b) and any attempt to deny the tenants' association the right to solicit members for such lawful activity would undermine the tenants' statutory right to form, join or participate in tenants' groups (Real Property Law, § 230) and would place an undue burden on First Amendment rights of association; in addition, petitioner may not enjoin the members of the tenants' association from displaying "Rent Strike" signs in the windows and on the doors of their apartments since the tenants' right to air grievances and to demand that legally created rights be accorded constitutes speech which is protected from prior restraint by the First Amendment [***2] notwithstanding its economically coercive effect; the tenants' constitutional rights of association and free speech in regards to such "public" areas of the building outweigh the landlord's already circumscribed private property rights but the draping or hanging of signs or banners out of windows over the building's facade must be prohibited pursuant to a prior appellate decision (see Alcoa Residences v Association of Tenants of Lincoln Towers, 28 AD2d 831).

 

1798 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Molly M. v. James F.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Bronx County


116 Misc. 2d 469; 455 N.Y.S.2d 700; 1982 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3900



October 14, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent alleged father filed a motion to dismiss the paternity proceeding filed by petitioner mother on the ground that the action was not commenced within two years of the child's birth. The mother filed a motion to order the alleged father to undergo a human leukocyte antigen (HLA) blood tissue test.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the mother was afforded an adequate opportunity to establish paternity and seek support. The court found that the mother was not provided with a sufficient opportunity to bring a paternity proceeding on behalf of her child. The court determined that her attempt to file a petition was frustrated by the inadequacy of the court's procedure made available to her by the state. The court ruled that the state's inadequacy did not bar the mother and her child from seeking financial support from the child's alleged father. Accordingly, in consideration of the best interests of the child, the court held that the mother's petition related back to that date when the mother first appeared at the court's department to commence the proceeding. The court further ruled that the N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 532 stated that the HLA test was available as a matter of right to both parties and that the result of the HLA test, based upon a proper certification the report alone, was admissible as evidence of the probability of paternity.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion of the mother that the alleged father be required to take the HLA blood issue test.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Children Born out of Wedlock -- Filiation Proceeding -- Limitation of Actions

1. Respondent's motion to dismiss a paternity proceeding seeking an order of filiation on the ground that the action was not commenced within two years of the child's birth as required by subdivision (a) of section 517 of the Family Court Act is dismissed since petitioner's contact with the Family Court Probation Department prior to expiration of the two years and subsequent failure of the department to process the petition until afterward tolled the Statute of Limitations and because petitioner was not provided with sufficient opportunity to bring a paternity proceeding due to the inadequacy of the procedure made available to her by the State.

Disclosure -- Blood-Grouping Tests -- Human Leucocyte Antigen Test as Probative Evidence of Paternity

2. A motion by petitioner mother for an order directing respondent to submit to a human leucocyte antigen (HLA) blood test for the purpose of establishing paternity is granted since pursuant to section 532 of the Family Court Act an HLA test is admissible as probative evidence of probability of paternity.

 

1799 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Laureano v. Koch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


116 Misc. 2d 287; 454 N.Y.S.2d 956; 1982 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3873



October 13, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tenants appealed the monthly rental increases on in rem housing determined by respondents, the City of New York and the Department of Housing Preservation and Development.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner tenants sought review and annulment of a determination of respondent, the Department of Housing Preservation and Development (HPD), by which rentals in tax foreclosed properties were increased by 50 to 108 percent per month. Petitioners were tenants in these properties when their private landlords defaulted in property tax payments and respondent, the City of New York, took over. The court granted the petition to the extent of annulling respondents' determination of rent increases. Tenants of in rem housing had a property interest in their own apartment units sufficient to trigger the rights and protections afforded by both the state Constitution and the New York City Charter. The city and its agencies, while acting as a landlord, did not have unlimited discretion to raise the rents. Respondents' actions in formulating massive rent increases for in rem tenants without published rules, regulations, standards or guidelines, without proper and lawful notice, and without fair and adequate opportunity for tenant consultation, explanation and contravention, were arbitrary, unlawful, unreasonable and unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition to the extent of annulling respondents' determination by which petitioners' rental charges were increased, of staying respondents from collecting such rent raises, and of declaring respondents' procedures for determining rent increases for in rem tenants administratively unlawful and state constitutionally infirm. An earlier order with respect to preliminary injunctive relief was made permanent.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Landlord and Tenant -- Abandoned Housing Taken Over by City of New York -- Due Process Rights of In Rem Tenants

The New York City Department of Housing Preservation and Development (HPD), while acting as a landlord of residential buildings taken over by the city after private landlords defaulted in property tax payments (Administrative Code of City of New York, § D17-4.0), does not have unlimited discretion to raise the rents pending the return of such properties to private ownership, such properties being removed from all rent protections when they first become in rem (Administrative Code, § Y51-3.0, subd e, par 2, cl [f]; § YY51-3.0, subd a, par [1], cl [a]) and then subject to rent stabilization upon transfer back to private ownership at whatever rent levels have been fixed by the city (Administrative Code, § YY51-3.3), since the original residential tenants of in rem housing have a property interest in their own apartment units sufficient to trigger in their favor important rights and protections afforded by both the State Constitution and the New York City Charter; at a minimum, tenants are entitled, as a due process requirement, to sufficiently detailed information [***2] to enable them to determine whether any rent raises are warranted and, if so, the grounds for such proposed increases and how they are to be calculated and tenants must also be permitted a fair opportunity for meaningful input both as to the percentage of an initial rent augmentation and as to its legal and mathematical viability thereafter; accordingly, the action of HPD in formulating massive rent increases for in rem tenants without published rules, regulations, standards or guidelines (see New York City Charter, § 1105, subd b), without proper and lawful notice and without fair and adequate opportunity for tenant consulation, explanation and contravention is arbitrary, unlawful, unreasonable and unconstitutional.

 

1800 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Manton v. Wilson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


115 Misc. 2d 1067; 455 N.Y.S.2d 65; 1982 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 3816



October 12, 1982 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The remaining branch of the cross motion and the plaintiff's motion are dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen filed a motion for injunctive relief and defendants, aide, director, employee, corporation, and State Office for the Aging (state office), filed a cross motion for dismissal, in an action involving the appropriation of state funds to the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was a not-for-profit, with various defendants holding positions in its organizational structure. Money was appropriated from the state for disbursement to the corporation through the state office. The citizen filed an action to stop the disbursement and void the contract, alleging that the appropriations were illegal because they were procured by the individual defendants. Defendants, who were proper parties, filed a motion to dismiss. The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, holding that there was no statutory violation pleaded that would justify the relief requested. Mere conclusions that violations of unconstitutional expenditures were being made were insufficient to state a cause of action. The law provided that no member of a company governed under the Community Senior Citizens Centers and Services Companies Law, N.Y. Priv. Hous. Fin. Law art. 7-A, could receive compensation for services, but there was no evidence that the corporation was being used for political activity or that any of its funds were expended to support any of the defendants.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint filed against them by the citizen in an action to stop the disbursement of state funds to a not-for-profit corporation.


HEADNOTES

Legislature -- Authority for Expenditure of Public Funds -- Judicial Review

1. In a citizen taxpayer action to declare void a $ 50,000 appropriation to be disbursed to defendant Sunnyside Intergenerational Services (SIS) through defendant State Office for the Aging, where plaintiff alleged that SIS is not an appropriate agency to receive such funds or that better agencies exist to receive such funds, there is no unconstitutional expenditure of funds asserted since the authority to appropriate and provide for the expenditure of public funds rests with the Legislature and not the courts and thus, the economic or political wisdom of any particular cost allocation is beyond the scope of judicial review.

Public Officers -- Appearance of Impropriety

2. In a citizen taxpayer action, plaintiff's allegation that an appropriation of State funds to be disbursed by the State Office for the Aging to Sunnyside Intergenerational Services (SIS) violates the provision of section 74 of the Public Officers Law which governs the appearance of impropriety of legislators and their staffs on [***2] the ground that one of two individual defendants who are incorporators and directors of SIS is a legislative aide to a defendant Assemblyman and the other is a former legislative employee is legally insufficient to support a cause of action since there is no evidence that SIS is being used for political activity or that any of its funds are expended to support the defendant Assemblyman or any current State or legislative employee.

Corporations -- Community Senior Citizens Centers and Services Company -- Compensation of Director

3. Salary payments made to defendant director of a not-for-profit corporation governed by the Community Senior Citizens Centers and Services Companies Law (Private Housing Finance Law, art 7-A) who is also an employee of said corporation do not violate the provision of that law which proscribes payment of any compensation to a person for his services as a director of a governed company (Private Housing Finance Law, § 356), since defendant is providing services as an employee as well to justify the salary she receives.

Public Officers -- Eligibility for Membership in Community Senior Citizens Centers and Services Companies

4. Plaintiff's [***3] contention that an expenditure of State funds by the State Office for the Aging to a not-for-profit corporation governed by the Community Senior Citizens Centers and Services Companies Law violates 9 NYCRR 2606.02 which prohibits membership in a governed company by elected public officials or members of their staffs on the ground that one of the directors of said corporation is an aide to a State Assemblyman is without merit since the regulation in question was intended to deal only with neighborhood preservation companies and the regulations of the State Office for the Aging contain no such restriction.
